Gold Level criteria Gold Level Exceptional Benefits for Climate (GL1). SERCOVA project 
meets the CCB criteria for Outstanding Climate Change Adaptation 
Benefits based on the project significant support to communities and 
biodiversity to adapt to anticipated climate change impacts and risks. 
SERCOVA project aims to restore ecosystem functions and create 
sustainable natural habitats, enhance biodiversity, and support 
community resilience in the face of climate change. SERCOVA project 
focuses on nurseries for native, food-trees, and Rare, Threatened, and 
Endangered (RTE) tree species through community engagement and 
collaboration. SERCOVA also focuses in improving community skills in 
adapting to climate risk and vulnerability, especially those reliant on 
agriculture and fishing activities, through livelihood diversification and 
trainings in climate-smart agriculture (CSA) and climate-smart fisheries 
(CSF). SERCOVA will also develop climate-resilient infrastructures and 
implement integrated natural disaster prevention and management 
systems. 
 
Gold Level Exceptional Benefits for Community (GL2). SERCOVA project 
meets the CCB criteria for Outstanding Community Benefits as most of 
the communities within the Project Zone qualified as Indigenous People 
and Local Communities (IPLC) and living below the national poverty line 
of IDR 2,592,657/month (USD 168/month). Out of 13 villages, only one 
village that has slightly higher income of IDR 3,000,000/month (USD 
194/month or USD 6.5/day) compare with the national poverty line. All 
the 12 other villages, have an average of IDR 1,645,833/month (USD 
106/month or USD 3.5/day). SERCOVA project aims to deliver significant 
well-being benefit to the IPLC through various program including 
employment opportunities, health services, education support, and 
financial assistance programs particularly for women, elderly, disabled, 
and orphans. 
 
Gold Level Exceptional Benefits for Biodiversity (GL3). SERCOVA project 
meets the CCB criteria for Outstanding Biodiversity Benefits as project 
activities contribute to the protection of the ecologically important IUCN 
Red List species in the project area. SERCOVA Project Zone is included 
as the Endemic Bird Area (EBA) and the Key Biodiversity Area (KBA). 
From 289 species (133 fauna, 156 flora) recorded from the project’s 
survey activities, around 31 species are included as IUCN Red List 
including species that are endemic to Maluku Islands and Wallacea 
Biogeography Region. SERCOVA Project Zone is estimated to hold over 
5% of the entire global population of the Endangered Purple-naped Lory 
(Lorius domicella) and the Vulnerable Salmon-crested Cockatoo 
(Cacatua moluccensis), among other IUCN Red List species.

1 SUMMARY OF PROJECT BENEFITS 
The Seram Climate and Conservation (SERCOVA) Project is an Improved Forest Management (IFM) 
project   that converts logging   activities   into   protected   forest   activities.   SERCOVA   is   being 
implemented on a concession area under a forestry license holds by a company named PT Strata 
Pacific.  
The total size of PT Strata Pacific concession is +73,365 ha, with +5,880 ha was designated for 
protection area, +2,009 was designated for non-effective area (non-logging area), and +66,076 ha 
was designated for effective logging area (covered with Primary Forest, Secondary Forest, and Non-
Forest Land Cover). The eligible area for Improved Forest Management (IFM) is 56,189 (i.e. Primary 
Forest   and   Secondary   Forest). The   overall   methodology   for   calculating   emissions   and 
removals/reductions  is  using  the Verified  Carbon  Standard  (VCS)  VM0010  methodology  for IFM. 
This methodology is applicable because the project activity includes planned timber harvest, and 
under the project scenario, forest use is limited to activities that do not result in commercial timber 
harvest  or  forest  degradation.  The  selected  carbon  pools  were  the  above  ground  biomass, 
deadwood,  and  harvested  wood  products.  The  above  ground  biomass  estimation  was  following 
non-destructive  sampling  using  30  nested-sampling  plots  (size  0.25  ha  each)  along  six  2-km 
transects. The number of plots has fulfilled the VCS requirement of 10% error and 95% confidence 
interval.  
SERCOVA Project lies on a unique ecosystem of Wallacea Region in the Seram Island categorized 
as Key Biodiversity Areas (KBA) and Endemic Bird Areas (EBA). Based on the recent studies by the 
Project, SERCOVA is home to more than 280 species of fauna and flora, with more than 8 species 
globally  threatened  species  of  the  IUCN
1
,  23  species  are  listed  under  CITES
2
 and  24  species 
protected  by  Indonesian  law.  Those  66 species (59 fauna and 7 flora) are  categorized as  High 
Conservation Value (HCV) species that possess high ecological important functions. The project is 
expected  to  achieve  exceptional  biodiversity  benefit  from  the  protection  of  the  species  and  its 
habitat. 
The  Project  is  also  expected  to  achieve  exceptional  community  benefit.  There  are  13  villages 
around the project area, where 12 villages’ income are below the national poverty line (around USD 
3.5 per day). Activities in this project are designed to contribute to poverty alleviation for those poor 
communities.  With  more  than  21,437  people  (9,881  women),  this  SERCOVA  project  is  targeting 
56%  of  the  entire  poor  population  in  the  East  Seram  District,  Maluku  Province.  Furthermore,  all 
local  communities  around  the  project  area  are  categorized  as  Indigenous  People  (IP)
3
 with  long 
histories  of  Tidore  and  Ternate  Kingdoms.  The  SERCOVA  project will  be able  to  generate 
outstanding community benefits from the positive contribution to the gender, indigenous people, 
and communities’ livelihood and wellbeing. 
The baseline scenario GHG emission removal and reduction were 50.4 million tCO
2
e (37 years) or 
1,361,337 tCO
2
e per annum, while the project scenario GHG emission removal and reduction is 
estimated  at  3,853,029  million  tCO
2
e  across  37  years  or  104,135.93  tCO
2
e  per  annum.

1.1 Unique Project Benefits 
The  project  aims  to  enhance  forest  management,  conserve  biodiversity,  and  improve  the 
resilience and wellbeing of Indigenous People and Local Communities (IPLC) through a series of 
targeted activities. The primary goals are to reduce greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions, conserve 
High  Conservation  Value  (HCV)  species,  and  improve  the  livelihoods  and  climate  resilience  of 
IPLCs.  SERCOVA  project  employs  a  multi-faceted  approach  that  includes  forest  rehabilitation, 
biodiversity   monitoring,   climate   adaptation   training,   and   the   promotion   of   climate-smart 
livelihood  options.  Special  emphasis  is  placed  on  prioritizing  vulnerable  groups  and  ensuring 
inclusive participation in decision-making processes.

1.2 Standardized Benefit Metrics 
                                                 
4
 Land  with woody vegetation that meets an internationally accepted definition (e.g., UNFCCC, FAO, or IPCC) of what constitutes a forest, 
which includes threshold parameters, such as minimum forest area, tree height and level of crown cover, and may include mature, secondary, 
degraded and wetland forests (VCS Program Definitions) 
5
 Reduced  emissions  from  deforestation  and  forest  degradation  (REDD) - Activities  that  reduce  GHG  emissions  by  slowing  or  stopping 
conversion of forests to non-forest land and/or reduce the degradation of forest land where forest biomass is lost (VCS Program Definitions) 
6
 Afforestation, reforestation and revegetation (ARR) - Activities that increase carbon stocks in woody biomass (and in some cases soils) by 
establishing, increasing and/or restoring vegetative cover through the planting, sowing and/or human-assisted natural regeneration of woody 
vegetation (VCS Program Definitions) 
7
 Improved  forest  management  (IFM) - Activities  that  change  forest  management  practices  and  increase  carbon  stock  on  forest  lands 
managed for wood products such as saw timber, pulpwood, and fuelwood (VCS Program Definitions)

2 PROJECT DETAILS 
2.1 Project Goals, Design and Long-Term Viability  
2.1.1 Summary Description of the Project (VCS, 3.2, 3.6, 3.10, 3.11, 3.13, 3.14; CCB, 
G1.2) 
The Seram Climate and Conservation (SERCOVA) Project is an Improved Forest Management (IFM) 
project  that converts logging  activities  into  forest protection activities.  SERCOVA  project  is  being 
implemented in a concession with a forestry license, holds by PT Strata Pacific for 45 years until 
November 2058 (SK.774/Menhut-II/2013). Since November 2013, PT Strata Pacific (SP) has legal 
rights to harvest natural trees within the concession and logged the natural trees according to the 
Working  Area  Map  (2016 – 2046)
15
, the  General  Work  Plan  (2016 – 2025)
16
 and  Annual  Work 
Plan (2016 – 2025)
17
 as approved by the government. In the absence of the project, the ±73,365 
ha concession  would  have  been  logged  and  releasing  GHG  emissions to  the  atmosphere. Since 
November  2021,  with  project  activities, SERCOVA  project has  been generating GHG  emission 
reduction  as  well  as GHG  emission removal through  the  implementation  of IFM  activities  from 
Logged to Protected Forest (LtPF). 
SERCOVA Project is in a unique ecosystem of Wallacea Region in Seram Island, the District of Seram 
Bagian Timur (SBT), the Province of Maluku. SERCOVA Project is home to more than 280 species 
of fauna and flora, with more than 8 species globally threatened species of the IUCN
18
, 23 species 
are listed under CITES
19
 and 24 species protected by Indonesian law (PT Gaia Eko Daya Buana, 
2024). Those 66 species (59 fauna and 7 flora) are categorized as High Conservation Value (HCV) 
species  that  possess  high  ecological  important  functions.  The Project  is  expected  to achieve 
exceptional biodiversity benefit from the protection of the species and its habitat. 
There are 13 villages that directly adjacent with the project area, of which 12 villages’ income levels 
are  below  the  national  poverty level  of  IDR 2,592,657/month or  USD  3.5/day (Badan  Pusat 
Statistik, 2023). Activities in this project are designed to contribute in poverty alleviation for those 
poor  communities.  With  more  than  21,437  people  (9,881  women),  this  SERCOVA Project  is 
targeting 56% of the entire poor population in the East Seram District, Maluku Province (PT Gaia 
Eko  Daya  Buana,  2024).  Furthermore,  all  local  communities  around  the  project  area  are 
categorized  as Indigenous People (IP)
20
 with  long histories of Tidore and Ternate Kingdoms.  The 
SERCOVA Project will  be able  to  generate  outstanding  community  benefits  from  the  positive 
contribution to the gender, indigenous people, and communities’ livelihood and wellbeing. 
 
                                                 
15
 Working Area Map is a map showing the designation of harvest block for 30 years and an integrated part of the concession license.  
16
 General Working Plan (Rencana Kerja Umum, RKU) is a 10-years work plan mandatory for license holder and approved by the Ministry of 
Environment and Forestry (MoEF). 
17
 Annual Work Plan (Rencana Kerja Tahunan, RKT) is an annual work plan mandatory for license holder and part of the RKU which approved 
by the MoEF.  
18
 IUCN (International Union for Conservation of Nature) is an international organization that has become the global authority on the status 
of the natural world (www.iucn.org). 
19
 CITES  (Convention  on  International  Trade  in  Endangered  Species  of  Wild  Fauna  and  Flora)  is  an  international  agreement  between 
governments to protect endangered plants and animals from the threats of international trade (www.cites.org). 
20
 Based on the Provincial Government of Maluku Regulation No. 14 year 2005 and the District Government of East Seram No. 1 year 2009 
on the Negeri Adat (customary nation). 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
8 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
SERCOVA Project is  designed  to  reduce  the  climate  risk  and  vulnerability  to  biodiversity  and 
community around the project zone. SERCOVA Project include activities that increase community 
awareness on climate risk & vulnerability, promote climate-smart agriculture, and provide access 
to  better  market  for  community  products  to  increase  community  adaptation  strategy  in  the 
changing  climate. The  Project  also  include  activities  that  restore  habitat  &  ecosystem  functions 
following  Ecosystem-based Adaptation  (EbA)  approach,  rehabilitate  degraded  land  using  native, 
fauna  food-trees,  and  RTE  (Rare,  Threatened,  and  Endangered)  tree  species  to  create  suitable 
habitat  for  species  and  reduce  the  extinction  risk  for  narrow  ecological  niches  such  as  endemic 
species  that  found  in  the  project  area.  Hence,  the  SERCOVA  project  will  be  able  to  generate 
outstanding climate change adaptation benefits from the positive contribution to biodiversity and 
community resilient.  
SERCOVA  project  area  is  the  eligible  area  for  IFM  activities  (+66,076  ha)  consist  of  primary, 
secondary,  and  non-forest cover (i.e.,  bareland,  shrubs).  SERCOVA  project  used the  VM0010 
methodology because the project activity includes planned timber harvest, and under the project 
scenario, forest use is limited to activities that do not result in commercial timber harvest or forest 
degradation. SERCOVA project crediting period was 37 years within project duration of 40 years. 
The project duration is renewable following the duration of the business license. 
The  estimated  total  baseline  GHG  emission  removal  and  reduction  was 50.4  million  tCO
2
e  (37 
years)  or  1,361,337  tCO
2
e  per  annum,  while  the  project  scenario  GHG  emission  removal  and 
reduction  is  estimated  at  3,853,029  million  tCO
2

2

tCO

SERCOVA  project  is  not  located  within  a  jurisdiction  covered  by  a  jurisdictional  REDD+  program. 
Until  now,  there  are two  jurisdictional  REDD+  program  at  provincial  level signed  by  the  national 
government (Ministry of Environment and Forestry, MoEF) under the national REDD+ program. Both 
jurisdictional REDD+ programs are funded by the World Bank, namely the East Kalimantan Province 
(East Kalimantan Jurisdictional Emission Reductions Program, EK JERP
21
) and the Jambi Province 
(Bio Carbon Fund Integrated Sustainable Forest Landscape, BioCF ISFL
22
).  
 
At national level, Indonesia has received Result-based Payment (RBP) for emission reduction within 
period 2014 – 2016  from  Green  Climate  Fund  (GCF)  for  USD  103.8  million,  and  period  2016 – 
2017 from Indonesia-Norway Partnership for USD 56 million
23
. Other than those programs, there 
are no other jurisdictional REDD+ program has been signed or implemented in Indonesia. Hence, 
SERCOVA Project that is located in Maluku Province and started in year 2021, is not covered by a 
jurisdictional REDD+ program.

2.1.4 Project Eligibility (VCS, 3.1, 3.6, 3.8, 3.18, 4.1; CCB Program Rules, 4.2.4, 4.6.4) 
According  to  the  VCS  Standard  4.7  in  Appendix  1,  the  project  activity  meets  the category 
requirements under Scope 14, defining the eligible Improved Forest Management (IFM) activity of 
the  AFOLU  project as  the  carbon  sequestration  and/or GHG emission  reduction  on  forest  lands 
managed for wood products (i.e., roundwood), resulting in increasing biomass carbon stock with 
the implementation of project activity. 
The project applies VM0010 Methodology for Improved Forest Management (IFM), v1.3, which is 
the latest version of the eligible methodology under the VCS Program. The methodology is applied 
in  full  in  the  project,  including  the  full  application  of  any  tools  or  modules  referred  to  by  a 
methodology. Based on the eligible IFM activities, the LtPF category includes practices that reduce 
net GHG emission through the conversion of logged forests to protected forests permanently, with 
the avoidance timber harvesting, protection and increasing biomass carbon stocks due to forest 
re-grows and/or continues to grow. 
In accordance with the deadline requirements of VCS Standard 4.7, AFOLU project shall initiate the 
process of pipeline listing (as set out in the Registration and Issuance Process) within 3 years prior 
to the project start date. As the project start date is on 8 November 2021, the pipeline deadline is 
on 8 November 2024, thus the project meets the requirements so far. The SERCOVA project will 
meet all CCB & VCS Standards requirements and all relevant deadlines.  
SERCOVA project has met all the project eligibility requirements of the VCS Standard (v4.7) and the 
CCB Program Rules (v3.1) as described and justified below: 
 
VCS 3.1. General Requirements 
1. SERCOVA project has met all applicable rules and requirements set out under the VCS Program 
and used  an  approved  methodology  that  went  through  the  methodology  development  and 
review process of the VCS. 
                                                 
24
 See Appendix 1 of the VCS Standard 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
10 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
2. SERCOVA project has followed the VCS principles taken from ISO 14064-2 on the relevance, 
completeness, consistency, accuracy, transparency, and conservativeness. 
3. SERCOVA project falls under the VCS Sectoral Scope 14 of the agriculture, forestry and other 
land  use  (AFOLU)  as  the  project  activity  is  being  implemented  on  land  with  legal  forestry 
license. 
4. Under the AFOLU, SERCOVA project activity is an eligible Improved Forest Management (IFM) 
activity, as the project activity increases carbon sequestration and/or GHG emission reduction 
on forest lands managed for wood products (i.e., roundwood) by increasing biomass carbon 
stocks through improving forest management practices. 
5. Under  the  IFM,  SERCOVA  project  activity  falls  under  the Logged  to  Protected  Forest  (LtPF) 
which  includes  practices  that  reduce  net  GHG  emission  through  the  conversion  of  logged 
forests to protected forests permanently. Protected forest will not only be maintained but also 
increased the biomass carbon stock due to the forest re-grows and/or continues to grow.  
6. SERCOVA project applies the latest version of the VM0010 Methodology for Improved Forest 
Management (IFM), v1.3. The methodology was applied in full by the project, including the full 
application of any tools or modules referred to by the methodology. No own-choice model or 
third-party default factors were used by the project outside of the VCS rules and requirements. 
7. SERCOVA  project  applies  with all  rules  and regulations  and will not  lead  to  violation of  any 
applicable law. 
VCS 3.6, 3.8 Project Design and Start Date 
1. SERCOVA project is a single installation of an AFOLU activity with one IFM project activity. 
2. SERCOVA  project  has  fulfilled  the  VCS  program  rules  and  requirements  by  also  conducting 
AFOLU  non-permanence  risk  analyses,  activity-shifting  and  market  leakage  assessments. 
have been conducted covering the entire SERCOVA project area 
3. SERCOVA  project  has  met  all  relevant-deadlines  requirements in  initiating  the process  of 
pipeline listing (as set out in the Registration and Issuance Process) within 3 years prior to the 
project start date. The project start date is on 8 November 2021, thus the pipeline deadline is 
on 8 November 2024.

2.1.9 Project Ownership (VCS, 3.2, 3.7, 3.10; CCB, G5.8) 
The SERCOVA project is owned by PT Strata Pacific (SP). PT SP is a company established in February 
9
th
,  2007 under  the Investment  Coordination  Body of the  Republic  of  Indonesia  with  NIB 
2702230091723. PT SP only has one forestry company, and no other concessions owned by PT 
SP or affiliated with the owner of PT SP.   
PT  Strata  Pacific  (SP)  has  the  legal  right to  control  and  operate  project  activities  based  on  the 
decrees granted by the Ministry of Environment and Forestry (MoEF) as a competent authority in 
forestry business. PT SP holds its forestry license since 2013 for logging activities through the MoEF 
Decree Number SK.774/Menhut-II/2013. Due to the carbon-project activities, PT SP then applied 
for a license conversion from IUPHHK-HA into forest utilization business permit (Perizinan Berusaha 
Pemanfaatan  Hutan,  PBPH)  to  allow  Multi  Forest-Utilization  (Multi  Usaha  Kehutanan, MUK) 
activities  for  converting  logging  activities  (i.e.,  timber  harvest)  into  non-logging  activities  (i.e., 
carbon). The MoEF granted the PBPH license in September 2021 through the MoEF Decree Number 
SK.687/MenLHK/Setjen/    HPL.0/9/2021. Furthermore,    the    MoEF    has    also    provided 
recommendation  letter  (Surat  Arahan)  on  August  26
th
,  2024  to  PT  Strata  Pacific  as  part  of  the 
approval  process  for  PBPH  MUK  Logged  to  Protected  Forest  (LtPF)  activities. Hence,  PT  SP  has 
demonstrated the legal rights to control and operate project activities in the project area.  
By  law,  the  Government  of  Indonesia  (GoI)  has  enacted  Law  No.  11/2020  on  Job  Creation  that 
mandate  all  forest-permit  holder  on  the  use  of  Multi  Forest-Utilization  (Multi  Usaha  Kehutanan, 
MUK) concept which allow logging activities (timber utilization) and non-logging activities including 
the utilization of non-timber forest product (NTFP) and environmental services such as carbon. The 
GoI has also enacted Law No. 7/2021 on Harmonization of Tax Regulation that mandates carbon 
tax for business sector that emits GHG emissions beyond the allowable cap set by the government, 
which trigger the domestic carbon market such as the Indonesia Carbon Exchange (IDX Carbon).  
IDX  Carbon  is  the  first  official  carbon  exchange  in  Indonesia.  It  was  developed  by  the  Indonesia 
Stock  Exchange  (IDX)  to  facilitate  carbon  trading  in  the  country  including  the  establishment  of 
Allowance  Market  (cap-and-trade  mechanism)  and  Offset  Market  (trading  of  carbon  units  from 
climate  mitigation  actions).  The  legal  foundation  of  IDX  Carbon  is  including  the  Presidential 
Regulation No. 98/2021 on Carbon Pricing in Indonesia, the MoEF Regulation No. 21/2022 on the 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
13 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Implementation of Carbon Pricing including mechanism for carbon trading and carbon offset, and 
the  Financial  Services  Authority  Regulation  (POJK)  No.  14/2023  on  the  Framework  for  Carbon 
Trading in Indonesia. As of June 2024, IDX Carbon has been trading 608,740 tCO2e with USD 2.4 
million transactions from 67 carbon service users
25
. These transactions reflect that business actors 
have the rights and ownership to trade carbon units generated from their business activities. The 
existing laws and regulations have set solid foundation in carbon trade business for private sector, 
including forestry companies.  
Furthermore, the GoI has enacted Government Regulation No. 23/2021 on Forestry Management 
which elaborate the Job Creation Law covering the concept of Multi Forest-Utilization (MUK), MoEF 
regulation  No.  8/2021  on  Forest  Management  which  operationalize  the  Government  Regulation 
No.  23/2021  covering  technical  aspects  for  MUK,  ecosystem  services  (i.e.,  carbon)  and  related 
activities,  and  the  MoEF  No.  7/2023  on Carbon  Trading  which  regulate  the  concept  of  carbon 
trading and its implementation mechanism in Indonesia. These regulations allow the forestry sector 
to further develop carbon trade business. 
Hence,  PT  Strata  Pacific  has  the  SERCOVA  project  ownership  based  on  the  existing  laws  and 
regulations, and has the legal right to control and operate the project activities (LtPF) based on the 
decrees granted by the competent authority, and has solid foundation in GHG emission reductions 
and/or removals business. 
 
2.1.10 Project Start Date (VCS, 3.8) 
Project start date  08-November-2021 
Justification  
Following the VCS definition, the project start date is the date on which 
activities  that  lead  to  the  generation  of  GHG  emission  reductions  or 
removals are implemented. 
 
The  main  step  of  logged  to  protected  forest  (LtPF)  activities  is  to  stop 
logging activities and protect the areas which have been legally planned 
to be harvested under the government-approved General Management 
Plan (Rencana Kerja Umum, RKU) and Annual Work Plan (Rencana Kerja 
Tahunan,  RKT). This  activity  has  been  done  by  the  Project  since 
November 8
th
, 2021.  
 
Therefore, the project start date is November 8
th
, 2021, which is the date 
where  logging  activities  were  stopped.  This  date is  then used  as  the 
baseline date   for   historical   reference   period   as   required   by   the 
methodological standards of the VCS.

2.1.14 Physical Parameters (CCB, G1.3) 
SERCOVA  Project is  at  the east  side  of  Seram  Island  in  Maluku Province.  Administratively, 
SERCOVA  Project located  in  Seram  Bagian  Timur (SBT) Regency,  Maluku  Province.  The  project 
area  lies  between  130
0
14’52”-130
0
38’57”  east  longitude  dan  03
0
30’16”- 03
0
33’05”  south 
latitude. The west side of the project area is adjacent to Gunung Tuntuan Protected Forest. The 
project location is a part of the global terrestrial ecoregion of “the Seram rainforests area” (Olson, 
2024). The physical parameters of the project are described below: 
Topography and Slope 
The project area is in a hilly area. Rivers in the project area are small rivers flowing in the valley 
between hills. Seismic activity is common in the project area. The elevation of the project area is 
8 - 825 meters above  sea  level.  The  further  away  from  the  sea  the  higher  the  elevation  of  the 
location. 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
16 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 
Figure 2-1. Map of the elevation within the PT Strata Pacific 
The Slope level in the project area is divided into four categories flat (slope 0-8%), ramps (slope 
9–15%), moderately steep (16–25%), and steep (slope 26–45%). The project area's topography 
varies  in  steepness. The  steep  level  in  the  project area  majority  is  moderately  steep at 35% of 
the project area, followed by steep at 31.88%, the flat is 16.67% of the project area and the ramp 
is only 16.20% of the project area
26
. In degree, minimum slope in the project area is 0 and the 
higher is 54.19 degree.  
 
Soil 
Soil types in the project area at the order level are dystropepts, eutropepts, rendolls, tropaquepts, 
tropopsamments, and tropudults, Dystropepts are the most common soil type in the project area. 
Total 76% of the area or 55,622 ha is Dystropepts. The second is tropaquepts with 11% or 7,875 
ha of the project area. While the rest of the others are less than 10% of the project area. 
Based  on  the  Geological  Map  of  Masohi  Sheet  Maluku  scale  1:  250,000  published  by  the 
Bandung  Geological  Research  and  Development  Centre,  the  geological  structure  in  the  project 
area  is  dominated  by  the  Kanikeh  Formation  and  Wahai  Formation.  Based  on  the  land  system 
maps, the project area dominated by other foothills, other ridges, volcanic foothills, alluvial plains, 
and montane wetlands,

Climate 
The  climate  in  the  project  area  is  tropical  marine  climate  and  seasonal  climate.  This  climate 
occurs because the project location is on an island surrounded by a vast sea. The sea strongly 
influences the climate in this area in harmony with the existing seasons.  
Based  on  the  rainfall  records,  known  that  according  to  Schmidt  &  Ferguson  (1951),  the  area 
belongs to rainfall type A which is characterized by dry months (<60 mm/month) for 4 months 
and wet months (>100 mm/month) for 7 months. The precipitation data in the project area can 
be  seen  in  the  table  below
27
.  Precipitation  in  the  project  area  varies  every  year.  Rainfall  in  the 
project  area  is  influenced  by  the  ENSO  (El  Nino-Southern  Oscillation)  phenomenon.  In  2023, 
when ENSO occurs the least rainfall is encountered.

Hydrology 
SERCOVA Project Area is located in the upper watershed of Tulung Arang. Rivers that are located 
and  flow  within  the  work  area  include  Bolifar  River,  Salas  River,  and  Loba  Besar  River.  These 
rivers flow from east to west with relatively slow flow rates and with a relatively slow flow rate and 
clear water, especially in the dry season. The rivers in this area are generally meandering, with 
muddy,  sandy  and  gravelly  riverbeds.  Riverbeds  are  muddy,  sandy  gravelly  to  rocky  and 
contaminated with sediment and organic organic material. River depths in the dry season range 
from 2.0m to 6.5 m. This work area is a forest area that plays a very large role in the infiltration 
of raindrops into the soil to reach the impermeable rock layer. This then moves horizontally to low 
places and emerges along the river as springs. Many springs are found along the river, especially 
during the rainy season.

Land Cover and Vegetation Type based on RKU 
The  natural  vegetation  of  Seram  is  tropical  lowland  evergreen,  semi-evergreen,  and  montane 
rainforest (Olson, 2024). The land cover in the assessment area consists of mature secondary 
dryland  forest,  young  secondary  dryland  forest,  and  non-forest  areas.  The  forest  area  in  the 
project area consists of Limited Production Forest, Permanent Production Forest, and Other Land 
Use Area.

The vegetation  structure  in  the  project  area  consists  of  two  categories  of  forest  areas  and  two 
non-forest areas. Forest areas consist of Mature secondary Dryland Forest and Young Secondary 
Dryland  Forest,  while  non-forest  areas  consist  of  Community  Plantation  and  Shrubs. Mature 
secondary  dryland  forests  also  exhibit  a  higher  number  and  density  of  trees  with  a  diameter 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
25 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
greater than 30 cm in comparison to young secondary dryland forests. Regarding carbon stock, 
Mature  secondary  dryland  forests  demonstrate  a  higher  carbon  stock  in  comparison  to  young 
secondary  dryland  forests. Concurrently,  non-forest  areas  are  characterised  by  grassland  and 
community plantations. These areas are open with a sparse tree density and a low carbon stock. 
The  forest  area  in  the  PT  Strata  Pacific  area  consists  of  Limited  Production  Forest,  Permanent 
Production Forest, and Other Land Use Area. 
In  the  the  forest,  the  big  tree  species  (class  A  dbh ≥30  cm)  such  as Homalium  foetidum, 
Canarium  vulgare,  and Diospyros  oblonga are  dominated  in the  forest  area.  The  medium  tree 
(class  B  dbh  15  cm ≤ 29.9  cm)  is  dominated  by Homalium  foetidum, Garcinia  dulcis,  and 
Diospyros  oblonga.  In  the  stakes  and  poles  (class  C  dbh  5cm ≤ 14.9  cm)  is  dominated  by 
Homalium  foetidum, Aglaia  sapindina,  and Garcinia dulcis. Homalium  foetidum has  the 
dominated of all species in each tree class. This indicates that this species is dominant. In non-
forest area or shrub vegetation reed grass (Imperata cylindrica) is a species that dominates in 
this area. while tree-level vegetation only grows in a few points with a very far distance. Then, in 
community plantation vegetation the species that dominate this area are teak (Tectona grandis) 
and sengon (Falcataria falcata). 
 
Figure 2-8. Map of the vegetation classes within the PT Strata Pacific 
In the project area, we found 156 tree species belonging to 40 families. Out of the 40 families 
identified, there are 6 dominating families including Myristicaceae, Myrtaceae, Phyllanthaceae, 
Lauraceae, and Burseraceae. Species from the Myristicaceae family were found as many as 16 
species,   Myrtaceae   13   species,   Phyllanthaceae   11   species,   Lauraceae   9   species,   and 
Burseraceae 8 species.

2.1.15 Social Parameters (VCS, 3.18; CCB, G1.3) 
Demography 
The carbon project will be implemented in several villages in East Seram Regency, Maluku Province, 
an area rich in cultural diversity, natural resources, and history. This region, once an oil mining area 
established by the Dutch Colonials and a site of wars during the colonial period and World War II, 
comprises 13  villages with  a  total population  of 21,051.  The population  data  reveals  a  range  of 
village  sizes,  from  small  villages  like  Boinfia  and  Solang  with  populations  of  241  and  428 
respectively, to larger ones like Bula with 12,890 residents. Gender distribution is balanced in most 
villages, although larger villages like Bula may show more variations, potentially due to migration 
patterns and economic activities. 
 
 
Figure 2-9. Map showing potentially impacted villages around the concession boundary.  
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
27 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 
Figure 2-10. Map showing land use and economic activities through participatory mapping.  
East Seram's ethnic composition is predominantly Seramese, divided into Seram Gunung (originally 
mountain  dwellers)  and  Seram  Pantai  (coastal  settlers),  with  the  Orang  Bati  subgroup  adding 
complexity  to  the  ethnic  landscape.  The  presence  of  migrants  from  Javanese, Bugis,  and Banda 
tribes further enhances the region's cultural diversity. Religiously, most of the population is Muslim, 
with a small Christian minority, reflecting the historical and social complexities of the area. These 
demographic   and   cultural   dynamics   have   significant   implications   for   the   socio-economic 
development and resource management of the villages involved in the carbon project. 
Livelihood 
Communities in the study villages depend on a variety of livelihoods. Agriculture and fisheries form 
the backbone  of the local economy,  with  sago  and fish  being  the main  commodities. Sago, as  a 
staple  food,  is  not  only  consumed  in  the  form  of  traditional  food  but  also  processed  into  other 
products  such  as  sago  flour  and  sago  plates.  In  addition  to  sago,  nutmeg,  cloves,  cacao,  and 
seasonal fruit crops are commodities in community plantations. Furthermore, some villages rely on 
crops that can be harvested more than once a year such as vegetables, bananas, and secondary 
crops. Fisheries, both in fresh and marine waters, provide a source of protein for the population as 
well as a source of income through the sale of catches.   
The  main  livelihood  for  most  villages  is  farming  (Table 2-8).  Exceptions  include  Boinfia,  where 
hunting and honey-seeking are the main livelihoods, and Hote, where fishing is predominant. Many 
villagers  also  engage  in  secondary  activities  to  supplement  their  income.  Common  alternative 
livelihoods include logging and hunting, seen in Kilmury, Selor, Gah, Salas, Dawang, Solang, Bellis, 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
28 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Waru,  Jembatan  Basah,  and  Rukun  Jaya.  Fishing  is  an  additional  livelihood  in  Kilmury,  Salas, 
Dawang, Hote, and Bula. 
In  Bula,  trading  and  employment  are  the  main  livelihoods,  with  fishing  and  farming  serving  as 
supplementary sources of income. This diverse range of economic activities highlights the adaptive 
strategies   of   these   communities,   allowing   them   to   navigate   and   thrive   amidst   varying 
environmental and economic conditions.

Wellbeing 
The  East  Seram  Regency  in  Maluku  Province  faces  significant  economic  challenges,  with  most 
villages  having  an  average  monthly  income  below  the  national  poverty  line  of  Rp  2,592,657. 
Villages  such  as  Kilmury,  Selor,  Gah,  Dawang,  Solang,  Boinfia,  and  Bellis  have  monthly  incomes 
ranging from Rp 1,250,000 to Rp 1,875,000, well below the poverty line. Even villages with slightly 
higher  incomes,  such  as  Salas  (Rp  2,075,000),  Hote  (Rp  2,020,000),  and  Jembatan  Basah (Rp 
1,990,000), remain below the poverty threshold, reflecting difficult economic conditions for many 
residents (Figure 2-11). 
 
Bula village stands out with a significantly higher average monthly income of Rp 3,000,000, which 
is above the national poverty line. This likely reflects better economic opportunities and economic 
diversification in the village, which also has a much larger population compared to other villages. 
With a  population  of  11,614, Bula likely has  better  infrastructure and wider access to  economic 
resources. 
Maluku Province itself is one of the provinces with the highest poverty rates in Indonesia, ranking 
fourth  with  a  rate  of  16.42%.  East  Seram  Regency,  as  part  of  Maluku  Province,  shows  an  even 
higher  poverty  rate  of  21.08%.  This  data  indicates  that  despite  some  villages  having  better 
economic conditions, most areas are still struggling with widespread poverty. 
Overall,  this  data  highlights  significant  economic  disparities  between  the  villages  in East  Seram 
Regency. The challenges include low average incomes far below the national poverty line and high 
poverty rates at both the regency and provincial levels. Efforts to improve economic conditions in 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
29 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
this  area  will  require  a  comprehensive  approach, including  improving  access  to  economic 
resources, education, and better infrastructure. 
 
 
Figure 2-11. Wellbeing in each village around PT Strata Pacific concession. 
 
Community Participation 
The  relationship  between  local  villages  and  PT  Strata  Pacific  shows  significant  variation.  The 
villages  experiencing  conflicts  with  PT  Strata  Pacific  are  Gah,  Boinfia,  and  Bellis.  These  conflicts 
are  primarily  due  to  issues  of  land  ownership  and  resource  utilization.  In contrast,  the  village  of 
Waru  supports  PT  Strata  Pacific,  likely  because  of  the  company's  involvement  in  community 
development  programs  that  benefit  the  villagers.  Other  villages,  such  as  Kilmury,  Selor,  Salas, 
Dawang, Solang, Hote, Jembatan Basah, Rukun Jaya, and Bula, display a neutral attitude towards 
PT  Strata  Pacific.  This  neutral  stance  may  be  due  to  a  lack  of  direct  contact  or  limited 
communication  with  the  company.  This  indicates  opportunities  for  PT  Strata  Pacific  to  enhance 
communication and collaboration with these villages. 
For a carbon project of PT Strata Pacific with communities around the project area, implementing 
Free, Prior, and Informed Consect (FPIC) is crucial for ensuring communities have a meaningful role 
in decisions affecting them. FPIC process that emphasized transparency, openness and community 
participation can prevent negativity in decision making and community involvement in the project. 
Village  meetings  and public  consultation have  being  implemented as  a  medium for socialization 
and evaluation of the project with the community following the IFC Performance Standard (2012). 
This  project  will  also  create,  train,  and  evaluate  Feedback,  Grievance,  Redressing  Mechanism 
(FGRM)  to  ensure  the  project  equality,  just,  transparency  and  continues  improvement  for 
community participations.

There are two boundaries in this SERCOVA Project, the Project Area boundary and the Project Zone 
boundary. Project Area boundary is defined as the geographic area in which the project activities 
are implemented. Project Zone boundary is defined as the geographic area encompassing project 
area  in  which the  implementation  of project  activities  directly affects land  and  associated 
resources, including activities such as livelihoods and community development. 
 
SERCOVA project activity that generate GHG emission reduction and/or removal is Improved Forest 
Management (IFM) activity that only eligible to be implemented on the area within PT Strata Pacific 
legal-permit   (i.e.,   concession)   and   legally-intended   to   be   harvested.   Following   VM0010 
methodology,  around +56,189  ha  out  of +73,365  ha  of  total  concession  size  is  eligible  as IFM 
project area. Hence, SERCOVA Project Area is +56,189 ha. 
 
SERCOVA project activity that not directly generate GHG emission reduction and/or removal, but 
generate  positive  impact  to  community livelihood  and  climate  resilient,  are  eligible  to  be 
implemented beyond PT Strata Pacific’s concession. Following SBIA  results  (PT  Gaia  Eko  Daya 
Buana, 2024), SERCOVA Project Zone is delineated based on the potentially impacted ecosystem 
services, community access to forest, livelihood activities, and cultural heritage (HCV4-6) within the 
village boundaries adjacent to the Project Area. Hence, SERCOVA Project Zone is 102,526 ha. 
 
In addition, the identified HCV and HCV areas (HCVA) are also shown in map below with detail HCV 
description described in SBIA report (PT Gaia Eko Daya Buana, 2024). 
 
 
Figure 2-12. Map showing Project Area and Project Zone of the SERCOVA Project.

2.1.17 Project Activities and Theory of Change (VCS, 3.6; CCB, G1.8) 
The SERCOVA Project aims to enhance forest management, conserve biodiversity, and improve the 
resilience  and  wellbeing of Indigenous  People and Local Communities  (IPLC) through  a  series of 
targeted  activities.  The  primary  goals  are  to  reduce  greenhouse  gas  (GHG)  emissions,  conserve 
High Conservation Value (HCV) species, and improve the livelihoods and climate resilience of IPLCs. 
The  project  employs  a  multi-faceted  approach  that  includes  forest  rehabilitation,  biodiversity 
monitoring,  climate  adaptation  training,  and  the  promotion  of  climate-smart  livelihood  options. 
Special emphasis is placed on prioritizing vulnerable groups and ensuring inclusive participation in 
decision-making processes. 
 
Theory of Change 
If  the  project  successfully  implements  IFM  practices,  conducts  regular  forest  patrols,  executes 
consistent rehabilitation activities, facilitates climate adaptation training, promotes climate-smart 
livelihoods, and prioritizes vulnerable groups in decision-making processes, then GHG emissions 
will  be  reduced,  HCV  species  and  habitats  will  be  conserved,  and  the  climate  resilience  and 
wellbeing of IPLCs will be improved. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
32 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 
Figure 2-14. SERCOVA Project Theory of Change 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
33 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
SERCOVA Project  is designed to deliver  the project  goal through  a  series  of objectives,  including 
below: 
1. Reduce GHG Emissions and Improve Forest Management 
o Implement Improved Forest Management (IFM) practices. 
o Convert logging activities to protected forest activities. 
o Conduct regular forest and fire patrols. 
2. Conserve Biodiversity and HCV Species 
o Identify and monitor HCV species. 
o Develop and implement biodiversity management plans. 
o Reduce threats from illegal wildlife trade and hunting. 
3. Enhance IPLC Resilience and Wellbeing 
o Provide climate adaptation training. 
o Promote climate-smart agriculture and fisheries. 
o Improve livelihood options through community enterprise development. 
4. Prioritize Vulnerable Groups 
o Ensure health and education services prioritize vulnerable groups. 
o Facilitate inclusive participation in decision-making processes. 
o Develop social safeguards to ensure transparent and just project implementation. 
 
SERCOVA project is designed to deliver the project objectives through a series of activities, including 
below: 
1. Forest Management and GHG Emissions Reduction 
o Activity 1.1-1.6: Apply for license conversion, develop work plans, and restructure company 
management to accommodate new business models. 
o Activity  2.1-2.6:  Identify  threats,  establish patrol  groups,  and  conduct  regular  patrols  to 
reduce illegal logging and uncontrolled fires. 
o Activity  3.1-3.6:  Identify  degraded  lands,  establish  nurseries,  and  conduct  tree  planting 
activities. 
2. Biodiversity Conservation 
o Activity  4.1-4.6:  Conduct  biodiversity  surveys,  develop  monitoring  plans,  and  support 
biodiversity-related research. 
o Activity  5.1-5.6:  Identify  threats  to  species,  develop  customary  laws,  and  support  law 
enforcement activities against illegal wildlife trade. 
3. IPLC Resilience and Wellbeing 
o Activity 6.1-6.6: Construct a training center, establish a knowledge management system, 
and facilitate cross-learning with universities. 
o Activity  7.1-7.4:  Conduct  climate  risk  assessments,  develop  adaptation  programs,  and 
provide training on climate-smart practices. 
o Activity 8.1-8.5: Conduct feasibility studies, develop business plans, and provide training 
on product development and market systems. 
4. Prioritizing Vulnerable Groups 
o Activity  9.1-9.5:  Assess  vulnerable  groups,  ensure  inclusive  participation,  and develop 
social safeguards. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
34 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
There are nine outputs in SERCOVA Project, including below: 
Output 1.  IFM  practice  is  legally  implemented  under  the  PBPH  MUK  that  convert  tree-logging 
into protection forest activities 
Output 2.  Threats from uncontrolled fires and illegal logging are reduced through regular forest 
patrol and law enforcement 
Output 3.  Degraded   land   and   forest   habitat   are   rehabilitated   through   assisted   natural 
regeneration (ANR) and tree planting 
Output 4.  Biological   diversity   and   High   Conservation   Value   (HCV)   species   are   identified, 
managed, and monitored regularly 
Output 5.  Threats   to   biodiversity   and   HCV   species   are   reduced   through   improved   law 
enforcement and community awareness 
Output 6.  Training & Knowledge Information Center ("Wallacea Center") is established to ensure 
good data management & transparency 
Output 7.  IPLC's understanding and capacity in climate change adaptation are increased 
Output 8.  IPLC's livelihood options and income are improved through increased revenue and/or 
reduced cost 
Output 9.  Vulnerable  groups  (i.e.,  woman-lead  household,  poorest  family,  orphan,  etc.)  are 
prioritized in benefiting from project 
 
There are three expected outcomes in SERCOVA Project, including below: 
Outcome  1: The  management  of  forest  is  improved,  GHG  emissions  are  reduced  and  removed 
through Improved Forest Management (IFM) practice in PT Strata Pacific concession 
Outcome  2: High  Conservation  Value  (HCV)  species  diversity  and  population  are  identified, 
maintained, monitored and sustainably conserved inside SERCOVA project zone 
Outcome  3: Indigenous  People  and  Local  Communities'  (IPLC)  climate  resilient  is  increased, 
wellbeing is improved, and vulnerable groups are prioritized through FPIC principles 
 
2.1.18 Sustainable Development Contributions (VCS, 3.17) 
The  mitigation  actions  carried  out  are  in  line  with  the  sustainable  development  target.  The 
Government of  the  Republic  of  Indonesia  has committed  to  the  Sustainable  Development  Goals 
(SDGs)  program,  in  accordance  with  the  declaration  in  September  2015  at  the  United  Nations 
General  Assembly.  This  is  also  proven  after  Indonesia  ratified  the  Paris  Agreement  through  Law 
Number  16  of  2016  concerning  the  ratification  of  the  Paris  Agreement  to  the  United  Nations 
Framework Convention on Climate Change (UNFCCC). SERCOVA Project supports the achievement 
of the SDGs as outlined in table below. All project data is available to support monitoring efforts.

Currently, the  average  income  of 12  villages (total  13  villages)  within 
SERCOVA  Project  Zone  are below national poverty  line. SERCOVA  Project 
supports   poverty   alleviation   for   IPLC through economic   assistance, 
employment, and higher-education  scholarships.  SERCOVA  Project  aims  to 
provide demonstrable livelihood benefits to surrounding communities. 
  
SERCOVA Project provides seedlings, training, and assistance to communities 
for  growing fruit-trees, implementing  climate-smart  agriculture  (CSA) and 
climate-smart fisheries (CSF) to ensure stable access to nutritious and safe 
food.  Furthermore,  the  Project  will  implement  livestock  assistance  program 
for deer, cow, goat, and/or chicken. 
 
Access to health facilities in several villages is constrained by the number of 
health  facilities  and  education  personnel. SERCOVA  Project  will  provide 
health   assistance which   mainly   targeting   elderly,   widow,   and   poorest 
community.  The  project  will  also  provide  food  supplement  for  toddler  to 
eradicate stunting.  
 
SERCOVA  Project  will  provide higher  education  assistance  (scholarship) 
which will enable Indigenous People and Local Communities (IPLC)s to have 
better access for higher education and increase educational opportunities.  
  
In  all  SERCOVA  Project  activities,  gender  mainstreaming  will  be  positively-
biased toward women empowerment. SERCOVA activities will ensure women 
able  to  participate,  and  actively-involved  in  the  decision-making  process. 
Furthermore,  SERCOVA  aim  to  provide local women’s group a  Micro,  Small 
and Medium Enterprises (MSMEs) assistance program.  
 
SERCOVA Project aims to employ local people, and provide decent training to 
increase local capacities to ensure decent work and contribute to economic 
growth. SERCOVA Project’s employment will also  provide  salary  and  related 
benefit including leave, health and life insurances following the government 
regulations and policies.

2.1.21 Benefit Permanence (CCB, G1.11) 
The SERCOVA Project is based on a 45-year initial license agreement, extendable one time with a 
maximum  of  the  same  period  with  initial  license  (45  years)  as  per  Indonesian  regulations.  The 
Project benefits are expected to extend beyond the license agreement. The Project is expected to 
maintain  and  expand  the  effective  status  of  the  forest  through  additional  licenses  or  increased 
state legal protection, recognizing the global importance of stored carbon stocks and biodiversity. 
Concurrently, efforts to restore degraded areas will enhance the project's resilience to fire threats 
and enable the restoration of natural vegetation over the course of the project.  
To  maintain  biodiversity,  the  project  will  carry  out  patrols  and  other  biodiversity  monitoring 
activities. These efforts will be documented using the SMART Patrol system as detailed in Section 
5.4. Moreover, community benefit activities are designed to be self-sustaining, managed by local 
communities  without  further  external  support.  The  community  development  activities  aim  to 
enhance  the  quality  of  life  for  affected  families  and  communities  through  a  comprehensive 
program. This program includes creating alternative livelihoods by offering training, providing initial 
or seed capital via a revolving fund, and opening markets for the products generated. Additionally, 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
40 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
it  focuses  on  health  and  sanitation  improvements  and  provides  educational  opportunities, 
particularly  for  youth  groups  to  access  higher  education.  Detailed  information  about  these 
community  development  activities  can  be  found  in  Section 4.4.  Ultimately,  the  project  aims  to 
mitigate  climate  change  by  enhancing  sustainable  forest  management,  conserving  biodiversity, 
and  empowering  local  communities  in  a 73,365-ha area  and  the  surrounding  communities  in 
Seram  Bagian  Timur.  Consequently,  the  SERCOVA  Project  will  contribute  to  more  sustainable 
regional  management  concerning  carbon  emissions,  biodiversity  conservation,  and  equitable 
community development. 
2.1.22 Financial Sustainability (CCB, G1.12) 
The SERCOVA Project and its proponent, PT Strata Pacific, is an established organization with stable 
cash flow. The project’s proponent has been operating in Seram for a number of years on forestry 
business and  is  neither seeking  for a loan nor  under debts for  SERCOVA  Project.  This  situation 
demonstrates a  sufficient  fund  is already  secured for  the  project development  and  long-term 
implementation. Documents  supporting  these investments and outlining the project’s financial 
feasibility and breakeven can be produced for the project auditor for inspection. 
 
2.2 Without-project Land Use Scenario and Additionality  
2.2.1 Conditions Prior to Project Initiation and Land Use Scenarios without the Project 
(VCS, 3.13; CCB, G2.1) 
The  Project  Area was  on  state-forest  land designated by the  Ministry  of  Forestry in 2013 
(SK.871/Menhut-II/2013) as Production  Forest  (HP) and Limited  Production Forest  (HPT),  which 
legally sanctioned as an area to be logged. Since mid-1990s, the project area has been repeatedly 
logged by various logging concession companies including PT Djayanti Group that operates until PT 
Strata Pacific granted its license in 2013. 
SERCOVA  Project  Area  was  covered  with  primary  and  secondary  dryland  forest  with  natural 
ecosystem  type  of  tropical  lowland  rainforests.  The  vegetation  structure  in  the  project  area  was 
formed by mature secondary dryland forest dominated by Homalium foetidum, Canarium vulgare, 
and Diospyros oblonga. These ecosystem type and vegetation structure echoing the ecosystem of 
Seram  Island  with  lowland  evergreen,  semi-evergreen,  and  montane  rainforest  (The  natural 
vegetation of Seram is tropical lowland evergreen, semi-evergreen, and montane rainforest (Olson, 
2024). 
PT  Strata  Pacific  holds  logging  concession  permit  (IUPHHK-HA)  in  2013 through  the Decree  of 
Minister of Environment and Forestry (MoEF) SK.774/Menhut-II/2013 since November 8
th
 2013 
(see Appendix 5). PT Strata Pacific has been operating based on the General Working Plan (RKU) 
and Annual Working Plan (RKT) which were approved by the government, with an average annual 
of 1,873 ha/year logging area or 122,513.23 m
3
/year logging volume (see Appendix 7) within the 
effective logging area of +66,076 ha (see Appendix 6). PT Strata Pacific continues to log the forest 
as evidenced in their reports (latest report of 2018 and 2019 are shown in Appendix 8 and 9). Due 
to Covid-19 pandemic, PT Strata Pacific experienced impact to their business that heavily rely on 
physical mobilities. This has made no timber harvesting activities occurred since early 2020. The 
situation  triggers a  different perspective  to  the  surrounding  community  where  some  of  the 
surrounding  communities  think  the  land  has  no  management  in  place  anymore. Consequently, 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
41 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
illegal logging activities and uncontrolled fires happened in the areas (see Figure 2-10 and Figure 
3-4). 
Prior to project initiation, the Project Area has been logged by PT Strata Pacific which owns the legal 
right to harvest. The project area was a complex mosaic of forest in conditions ranging from intact 
to highly degraded areas due to logging activities. In the absence of the project, the Project Area 
would  have  been  legally  logged  with  an  average  annual  of  1,873  ha/year  logging  area  or 
122,513.23 m
3
/year logging volume, showed on their government-approved RKU and RKT (RKU 
2016-2025 is  shown  in  Appendix 7),  in  addition  to  the  illegal logging  activities  and  uncontrolled 
fires  that  happened  due  to  COVID-19  pandemic. The  baseline  scenario  along  with  the  range  of 
potential land use scenarios are further discussed in Section 3.1.4. 
Considering PT Strata Pacific is the owner of SERCOVA project and the sole forestry license holder 
(PBPH  MUK)  to  operate  within  their  concession,  it  is  confirmed  that  the  project  has  not  been 
implemented to generate GHG emissions for the purpose of their subsequent reduction or removal. 
2.2.2 Most-Likely Scenario Justification (CCB, G2.1) 
The most-likely scenario that would happen in the project area is that the area would be subjected 
to  forest  management  practice  which  involves  planned  timber  harvest  for  commercial timber. 
Please  refer  to  section  3.1.4  and  3.1.5  for  a  justification  of  the  land  use  scenario  without  the 
Projects and the other land use scenarios considered. 
2.2.3 Community and Biodiversity Additionality (CCB, G2.2) 
With respect to the potential community activities described in Section 2.1.11, some of the major 
obstacles to the implementation of these activities identified by communities themselves (during 
workshop discussions and in household surveys) are 1) a lack of expertise, technical knowledge 
and skills, 2) lack of access to external markets and potential partner organizations, and 3) a lack 
of  start-up  capital  and  options  for  microfinancing.  The  project  will  seek  to  either  provide  these 
services directly or leverage them from elsewhere, as appropriate. There are not known to be any 
alternative mechanisms by which project zone communities could receive similar assistance at the 
present  time.  The  without-project  scenario  entails  the  continuation  of  commercial  logging  and 
mosaic planting operations within the project area, with concomitant negative impacts on native 
biodiversity.  
Nevertheless, through FPIC process, stakeholders agreed to support SERCOVA project from logged 
to  protected  forests (see  Appendix  18).  By  converting  the legal  permit  from  logging  to  multi-
business (MUK) protection forest, the habitats and natural ecosystems will have legal protection. 
The protection of the project area from future disturbances, together with potential rehabilitation 
activities under the project, can be expected to generate positive impacts for fauna & flora diversity 
which would not have occurred under the without-project scenario including the ecosystem function 
in the project area.  
2.2.4 Benefits to be used as Offsets (CCB, G2.2) 
None of the expected community and biodiversity benefits are intended to be used as offsets. Only 
the climate benefits derived by the project will be used as offsets.

CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
2.3 Safeguards and Stakeholder Engagement   
2.3.1 Stakeholder Identification (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB G1.5) 
As SERCOVA Project was originally a logging concession owned by PT Strata Pacific, communities 
that have been involved in previous logging business are automatically identified as beneficiaries. 
Since  PT  Strata  Pacific  has  been  working  in  the  area  since  2013,  local  communities  and 
stakeholders are pretty much identified.  
 
However,   since   SERCOVA   project   is   not   a   logging   business,   we   did   another   stakeholder 
identification to better understand the perspective from stakeholder including potential impact and 
inclusive process in project engagement. The Free, Prior, and Informed Consent (FPIC) principles 
are   practiced   during   the   process,   including   emphasize   on   Indigenous   People   and   Local 
Communities  (IPLC),  women,  and  minorities.  As  part  of  the  FPIC  process,  public  consultation  on 
SERCOVA Project was conducted and gain consent from all stakeholder (please see Appendix 18). 
Ongoing IPLC engagement will still be conducted during the project implementation as FPIC is an 
ongoing process and not one-time event.  
 
For  Stakeholder  Identification, SERCOVA  Project conducted  studies using  social  approach  and 
stakeholder mapping. The process of stakeholder mapping was identifying stakeholders potentially 
impacted by the carbon project involves the following steps: 
1. Mapping the Project Area & Project Zone: We begin by analyzing the geographical area where the 
project  activities  will  take  place,  considering  local  communities,  landowners,  and  ecosystem 
services. Delineating the Project Area and Project Zone provide an understanding of the potentially 
impacted  community  from  legal  and  spatial  perspectives which  then  followed  up  with  ground 
assessment on the potentially impacted stakeholder. 
2. Engagement with Local Authorities: We then collaborate with local government and administrative 
bodies  to  identify  relevant  community  leaders,  local  organizations,  and  institutions  involved  or 
affected  by  land  use,  environmental  policies,  and  socio-economic  activities. This  to  understand 
from interested parties from the government and local authorities’ perspectives, especially party 
who will be affected by the project. 
3. Community  Consultation:  Meetings  and  consultations were held  with  local  communities  and 
indigenous groups to gather input on how the project might affect their livelihoods, land rights, and 
cultural  practices. We  identified  all  communities  that  currently  or  historically  have  access or 
dependency to Project Area. 
4. Identification   of   External   Stakeholders:   We   identify   broader   stakeholders,   such   as   NGOs, 
environmental groups, and industry players, that may have an interest in the project's outcomes, 
either through environmental impact or socio-economic benefits. 
5. Review of Regulatory Requirements: We examine national and regional regulations to identify any 
governmental agencies or authorities that will be impacted by or have oversight of the project. 
6. Stakeholder Mapping Tool: A stakeholder mapping tool or matrix is used to categorize stakeholders 
based on their level of influence, interest, and the degree to which they may be impacted by the 
project.  
 
This comprehensive process ensures that all stakeholders, both direct and indirect, are identified 
and engaged appropriately. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
43 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
2.3.2 Stakeholder Descriptions (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G1.6, G1.13) 
In general, we categorize stakeholders into three groups: government, business entities, and the 
community. The stakeholder identification process has been explained in previous section. From 
this,  we  identify  stakeholders  and  their  relationship  to  the  project  based  on  these  stakeholder 
groups. Detailed information on stakeholders can be found in Appendix 1. This table also explains 
the   relationship   of   each   stakeholder   to   the   carbon   project,   generally   showing   that   the 
government's  involvement  is  more  related  to  the  project's  alignment  with  the  local  and  central 
government's development agenda. In contrast, the relationship with business entities is based 
on  business  interests  that  may  interfere  with  the  project's  progress.  The  relationship  with  the 
community can generally be described in terms of the impacts, both positive and negative, that 
the project may have on the community. 
2.3.3 Stakeholder Access to Project Documents (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G3.1) 
The  SERCOVA  project  has  conducted  multiple  community engagement  sessions  where  the 
project's  goals  and planned  activities were  explained  and  discussed.  To  support  these  efforts, 
brochure  and  report in Bahasa  Indonesia were created, summarizing the project’s objectives, 
implementing organizations, and key principles such as biodiversity, carbon sequestration, global 
warming, and the principles of Free, Prior, and Informed Consent (FPIC). The brochure and report 
were distributed to community leaders, who were then tasked with sharing them with the broader 
community. Additionally, the project plans to make documentation accessible through the project 
website and other channels like community notice boards in villages. In a long run (between Year 
5-10  of  project), SERCOVA  Project  plans  to construct  a  Knowledge  Management  Center (called 
Wallacea Center) as a central hub for information, training, and community events that can be 
access by the community and even greater stakeholder.  
2.3.4 Dissemination of Summary Project Documents (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G3.1) 
As noted in section 2.3.3, the project's start date, description, and background information on key 
concepts  have  been  translated  into Bahasa  Indonesia and  shared  with  communities  through 
brochures. Moving forward, summary information from key project documents will be prepared in 
Bahasa Indonesia and distributed to communities in printed form. These documents will include, 
among  other  things,  summaries  of  the  social  baseline  assessment,  the  project  description  (PD), 
monitoring reports, a schematic of the project's grievance and redress mechanism, and any other 
relevant documentation that may be requested by the communities. It is also planned that in the 
future,  the  construction  of  Wallacea  Center  will  able  to  be  the  medium  to  disseminate  project 
information including the summary of Project Documents.  
2.3.5 Informational Meetings with Stakeholders (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G3.1) 
The project began conducting informational meetings with stakeholder in 2020 as the effect for 
Covid-19 pandemic. The meeting explained potential change to the of business model, including 
the potential impact to stakeholders. Significantly less meeting with communities were happened 
during 2020 and 2021 due to the Covid-19 pandemic. Communication with the government and 
other  business-partners  stakeholders  were  still  continued even  during  the  pandemic, as the 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template

company needs to take corporate actions to maintain business. When the company decided to 
convert  logging  business to carbon  business,  intense  communication  happened  that  resulted 
into  the  changes  from  logging  license  (IUPHHK-HA)  into  forestry  multi-business  license  (PBPH 
MUK)  in  2021.  Since  2022,  more  follow-up  meetings  were  happened  to  understand  the

2023, a thorough assessment on ecosystem service feasibility study was conducted, along with 
other forestry-related assessment (for PBPH MUK), which resulted that the changes of PT Strata 
Pacific business model from Logged to Protected Forest (LtPF) is feasible. The Feasibility Study 
(FS)  also  emphasize  the  needs  of  community  development  and  potential  revenue  stream  from

2.3.6 Risks from the Project and No Net Harm (VCS, 3.18, 3.19) 
In the SERCOVA Project, Risks from the project and no net harm follows the implementation steps 
outlined below:  
1. Risk  Identification:   We  identify  potential  risks,  both  natural  and human-induced,  that  may  arise 
from  project  activities  throughout  its  lifetime.  These  risks  may  relate  to  environmental  impacts, 
community interactions, regulatory challenges, and project operations. Common risks include: 
o Natural  Risks:  Climate  variability  (e.g.,  extreme  weather  events,  floods,  droughts),  fires, 
pest outbreaks, and land degradation. 
o Human-Induced   Risks:   Social   conflicts,   land   disputes,   illegal   logging,   unauthorized 
deforestation, and negative community perceptions of the project. 
2. Preventive  and  Mitigation  Measures:   For  each  identified  risk,  we  describe  the  preventive  or 
mitigation  measures  implemented  to  ensure  that  these  risks  are  minimized  or  avoided.  These 
measures include: 
o For  Natural  Risks:  Developing  climate-resilient  practices,  monitoring  weather  patterns, 
creating firebreaks, and implementing adaptive management strategies. 
o For   Human-Induced   Risks:   Engaging   stakeholders   through   regular   consultations, 
establishing land use agreements, strengthening law enforcement, and raising awareness 
of the project's benefits through community outreach programs. 
3. Risk Monitoring: A continuous monitoring system is implemented to track potential risks throughout 
the project  lifecycle.  This  ensures early  identification  of issues  and  a  quick  response to  mitigate 
any harm. 
The  Project  Risks  Table  (Appendix  3)  provides  detailed  risk  assessment  information,  including 
the  type  of  risk,  its  likelihood,  severity,  and  specific  mitigation  strategies  tailored  to  each 
identified risk. By implementing these preventive and mitigation strategies, the Sercova project 
ensures minimal adverse effects and achieves No Net Harm in terms of environmental and social 
impact. 
2.3.7 Community Costs, Risks, and Benefits (CCB, G3.2) 
Government and community stakeholders have been involved from project start through the FPIC 
process.  At  the  initial  stage,  the  meeting  with  the  community  began  with  an  in-depth  and 
comprehensive  explanation  of  the  project.  Explanations  of  project  activities  that  are  likely  to 
provide costs, risks and benefits to the community are explained and, in this process, we provide 
freedom for the community to provide responses to the explanations we provide. This response 
is also an  input  for  the  project  in  developing the costs, risks and  benefits that  will  be  provided 
from  the  project  to  the  community.  This  feedback  is  important  as  a  participatory  part  that  is 
carried out from the beginning of the project.  
 
Input from the community at the beginning of the project we get some community expectations 
from this project in the form of benefits and risks that they might receive from the presence of 
the project, benefits and risks are present based on the reflection of community activities related 
to the project and the impact they have felt from the presence of another company in the area 
around their settlement.

2.3.8 Information to Stakeholders on Validation and Verification Process (VCS, 3.18.6, 
3.19; CCB, G3.3) 
Participating  communities  will  be  informed  about  the  process  of  CCB  and  VCS validation  and 
verification schedule and any required participation from their residents. Information have been 
shared  among  communities  as  a  preparation  that  there  will  be  Validation  &  Verification  Body 
(VVB) coming to validate and verify SERCOVA Project activities. Information were shared during 
multiple community workshops and materials such as brochures. Further information will always 
be updated along the VVB process including when the project validated and verified. Prior to VVB 
visit, the  project  team will  ensure village  leaders,  customary  leaders,  government,  and  other 
stakeholders are aware, engaged, and willing to participate in the process.

information including the summary of Project Documents.  
 
2.3.9 Site Visit Information and Opportunities to Communicate with Auditor (VCS, 
3.18.6; CCB, G3.3) 
Approximately three weeks before the implementation of CCB and VCS validation and verification 
activities,  the  project  team  will  inform  the  communities  in  the participating villages.  The 
preparation process will include the following steps: 
1. Preparing validation and verification materials, such as the PD document, all supporting 
documents,   and   a   summary   of   validation   and   verification   information   for   the 
communities. 
2. Approaching and explaining the activities to the leaders of the engaged villages. 
3. Arranging   meetings   with   community   beneficiaries   of   the   project   activities,   with 
adjustments made to meet the needs of the auditor during the audit process. 
4. Creating a visiting route that considers the distance, time, and transportation between 
villages and the forest area within the project area. 
 
Future  visits  to  communities  by  external  validation  and  verification  auditors  will  be  organized 
jointly  with SERCOVA  staffs  at  field  level and community  representatives who  will  assist in 
informing  the  wider  community  about  the  visits. Communities will  be  encouraged  to  speak 
directly  to  the  auditors,  and  to  freely  voice  any  opinions  they  hold  regarding  the  project.  The 
auditor  will  be  able  to  ask  questions  of  all  stakeholders  regarding  Free, Prior,  and  Informed 
Consent (FPIC) consultations engagement with the project.
