5.1.3 Without-project Scenario: Biodiversity (CCB, B1.3) 
Without  the project  scenario,  the  biodiversity  habitat  in  the  project  area  will  become  a  logging 
area.  Logging  activities  will  lead  to  reduced  forest  cover  in  the  project  area  and  will  impact  on 
flora  and  fauna  populations.  This  activity  will  lead  to  further  access  into  the  project  area. 
Furthermore, this road will become an access for hunters to hunt animals in the project area.  
Access to the project area is used by the surrounding community to create plantations within the 
project area. Some of the existing community plantations are in the form of agroforestry systems. 
Without the project scenario, the management of the community plantation in the project area 
is  not  sustainable.  Some  of  the  unsustainable  practices  are  land-burning  activities  in  areas  of 
former community plantations that are no longer in use. This would cause the value of biodiversity 
to decline or be completely lost. 
5.2 Net Positive Biodiversity Impacts  
5.2.1 Expected Biodiversity Changes (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B2.1) 
The  Seram  Climate  and  Conservation  (SERCOVA)  project  is  an  Improved  Forest  Management 
(IFM)  project that convert  logging activities into  protected  forest activities.  The eligibility  of  this 
methods  please  see  section  xx.  Under  the  project  scenario,  forest  in  the  project  area  will  be

Biodiversity element Fauna diversity 
Estimated change Gradual dispersal and increase of fauna species in the project 
area. 
Justification of change It is anticipated that the abundance of fauna in the project 
area will increase due to the project activities. The positive 
impact of the project can be determined by comparing the 
abundance of RTE fauna species in the project area to the 
number previously identified. This will be accomplished by a 
regular patrol team that will patrol the project area. The 
monitoring of fauna will be conducted to monitor the 
population of RTE fauna species. In addition, Livelihood 
improvement and community awareness are also done to 
reduce poaching activities in the project area. 
 
Biodiversity element Flora diversity 
Estimated change Gradual  dispersal  and  increase  of  flora  species  in  the  project 
area 
Justification of change It  is  anticipated  that  the  abundance  of  flora  species  in  the 
project  area  will  increase  due  to  the  project  activities.  The 
positive impact of the project can be determined by comparing 
the  abundance  of  RTE  flora  species  in  the  project  area  to  the 
number  previously  identified.  This  will  be  accomplished  by  a 
regular  patrol  team  that  will  patrol  the  project  area  and  the 
planting activities. The  monitoring of  flora  will  be conducted  to 
monitor   the   population   of   RTE   flora   species.   In   addition, 
Livelihood  improvement  and  community  awareness  are  also 
done to reduce illegal logging activities in the project area. 
 
Biodiversity element Natural Ecosystem 
Estimated change Reduced factors that contribute to species extinction and 
biodiversity loss 
Justification of change The project will be protecting the ecosystem and stopping 
disruptive activities as in the previous activity. These programs 
are expected to have significant positive impact on the 
ecosystem within the nearby project area, which will create a

Estimated change Reduced deforestation and forest degradation

forest  area.    Implementation  of  this  activity  will  significantly 
reduce forest canopy clearance and regenerate deforested and 
degraded areas. Planting also conducted in the degraded forest 
in the project area.  
 
5.2.2 Mitigation Measures (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B2.3) 
Based on the assessment conducted by the project team, there are no expected negative impacts 
of the project on biodiversity and ecosystem. Therefore, no mitigation measures are required.  
5.2.3 Net Positive Biodiversity Impacts (CCB, B2.2, GL1.4) 
The project will give positive impacts to biodiversity in the project area. The change activity from 
logging to protection will have a positive impact on existing biodiversity.  
5.2.4 High Conservation Values Protected (CCB, B2.4) 
The initial survey found that there are five HCV categories found in the project area. The 
information can be seen in section 5.1.2. they are namely: 
- HCV 1: Species diversity 
o Rare, threatened, and endangered species 
o Endemic species 
o Areas that contain habitat for viable populations of endangered, restricted-range or 
protected species. 
o Areas that contain habitat of temporary use by species or congregations of species 
- HCV 2: Ecosystems and mosaic ecosystems at the landscape level 
o Large natural landscapes with capacity to maintain natural ecological processes 
and dynamics. 
o Areas that contain two or more contiguous ecosystems 
o Areas that contain representative populations of most naturally occurring species 
 
The main activities of the project are protected forest and the biodiversity in the project area. The 
project  contributes  to  preserving  and improving  the  area  and  quality  of  forests  and  natural 
ecosystems, The  project  will  be  reducing  threats  to  biodiversity  populations.  With  all  these 
activities, the project will have a significant positive impact on HCV 1 and HCV 2. Infrastructure

such  as  existing  basecamps,  guard  posts,  fire  towers  and  nurseries  will  be  improved  without 
opening new areas and additional infrastructure if needed will be done in open areas so as not 
to degrade the forest area.

5.2.6 Invasive Species (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B2.5) 
Project  activities  will  not  use  an  invasive  species,  although  some  species  are  identified  as 
invasive.  The  initial  survey  discovered  289  species  in  the  project  area,  25  alien  species  and  6 
invasive species have been identified.  Alien species are plants, animals or other organisms taken 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
180 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
beyond their natural range by people, deliberately or unintentionally (also termed ‘introduced’ or 
‘non-native’ species); while invasive species are introduced species that become destructive to 
the environment or human interests (IUCN, 2018)
46
. Although some alien species and invasive 
species are found in the project area, some mitigation will be done so that these species do not 
have a negative impact.

species 
Mitigation measures to prevent the spread or continued existence of

Domestic dog  
(Canis lupus) 
Prevention:  
Install signboards with information on the prohibition of hunting with hounds

ecosystems. 
Surveillance: 
Establish patrol teams and conduct surveillance in the project area regularly 
and systematically to tackle any findings of invasive alien species, including 
domestic dogs. 
Translocation 
Relocate domestic dogs that stray within the project area and evacuate 
them to shelters.

area.

5.2.7 GMO Exclusion (CCB, B2.7) 
No genetically modified organisms (GMOs) will be used in the project. In addition, planting 
activities do not make use of seeds derived from GMOs. 
5.2.8 Inputs Justification (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B2.8) 
The project activities will not use fertilizer, chemical pesticides, biological control agents nor 
other similar inputs will be used in the project’s restoration efforts.

5.2.9 Waste Products (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B2.9) 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
182 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Project activities will generate waste products from general activities. Waste generated by human 
activities (domestic waste) in field offices, basecamp, and guard posts is one example of potential 
waste generated by project activities. Domestic waste includes solid waste such as plastic waste, 
used  cans,  used  plastic  packaging,  Styrofoam,  paper,  and  food  waste,  as  well  as  liquid  waste 
such  as  soapy  water,  detergent  water,  oil,  and  faeces. Domestic  waste  in  the  location  will  be 
separated  into  organic  and  non-organic. Moreover, there  is  the  possibility  of  waste  from 
operational  activities  such  as  used  generator  oil,  used  vehicle  or  engine oil,  gasoline  or  diesel 
spills, and used batteries. In line with the company’s Environmental Management and Monitoring 
Plan  (UKL/UPL),  the  project  will  develop  a  Standard  Operating  Procedure  (SOP)  for  waste 
management.  The  project  will  apply  the  3R  concept  (Reduce,  Reuse,  Recycle),  which  involves 
reusing waste that can still be used or has other functions, reducing everything that causes or 
generates waste, and recycling waste into a product or item that can be useful.

5.3.2 Net Offsite Biodiversity Benefits (VCS, 3.19; CCB, B3.3) 
Net  offsite  biodiversity  benefits  are  expected  to  be  positive  due  to  the  project  activities.  The 
project  focuses  on  the  protection  of  biodiversity  and  improvement  of  biodiversity  habitat, 
especially for RTE and endemic species.  
The  project  scenario  will  provide  positive  biodiversity  impact  in  the  project  area  and  its 
surroundings.   Considering   the   project   activities   in   forest   patrol,   community   awareness, 
monitoring species and habitat, the project will provide more favourable conditions for species 
and habitat conservation.

species are monitored collaboratively with community and other stakeholders. Furthermore, the

5.4.2 Biodiversity Monitoring Plan Dissemination (CCB, B4.3) 
The results of biodiversity monitoring are disseminated in three ways. First, the project proponent 
team will regularly publish information sheets and display them on the village information boards. 
Information will also be disseminated orally in community meetings and in local schools. Second, 
by distributing annual reports to relevant government stakeholders (MoEF, BKSDA, the Provincial 
Forestry  Agency,  Forest  Management  Unit,  and  Environmental  Agency).  Third,  by  consistently 
sharing  information  via  social  media  and  the  project’s  website. Sharing  information  with 
stakeholders  is  one  of  the  mitigation  efforts; the data  will  be useful  for the stakeholders  to be 
able to guide the implementation of appropriate mitigation measures. 
5.5 Optional Criterion: Exceptional Biodiversity Benefits  
The project aims to achieve exceptional biodiversity benefits and be validated to the Gold Level 
based on the presence of ecologically important IUCN Red List species (GL3) in the project 
area. 
5.5.1 High Biodiversity Conservation Priority Status (CCB, GL3.1) 
A  total  of 67  species  of  fauna  and  flora  found  in  this  survey  belonged  to  the  Vulnerable, 
Endangered, and Critically Endangered categories according to the IUCN Red List, Appendix I and 
II  of  the  Convention  on  International  Trade  in  Endangered  Species  of  Wild  Fauna  and  Flora 
(CITES), protected by the Government of Indonesia (MoEF Regulation No. P106/2018), migratory 
species, and/or has a limited distribution, in this case limited to Seram Island and small islands 
in around Maluku (Wallacea).rBased on the IUCN Red List, there are 8 fauna and flora species 
included in the VU, EN and CR categories. Currently, mammals and flora are the most numerous 
with  3  species  each.  Based  on  CITES,  23  species  are  included  in  Appendix  I  and  II  categories. 
From  the  list  of  protected  species  by  the  Ministry  of  Environment  and  Forestry,  there  are  26 
species. The largest number of HCV 1 categories comes from the list of fauna species that have 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
185 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
a  limited  distribution,  namely  28  species.  In  migratory  species,  there  are  15  species  of  bird 
included in this category. The survey that was conducted found 5 species of biodiversity that are 
included in the endangered category according to the IUCN Red List. The species is Purple-naped 
Lory (Lorius domicella), Black-bearded Flying Fox (Pteropus melanopogon), Burmese Rosewood 
(Pterocarpus  indicus),  Red  Sanders  (Pterocarpus  santalinus),  and  Teak  (Tectona  grandis).  The 
initial  survey  also  found  2  species  categorized  as  vulnerable  by  The  IUCN  Red  List  namely, 
Salmon-crested  Cockatoo  (Cacatua  moluccensis)  and  Javan  Deer  (Rusa  timorensis).  Salmon-
crested  Cockatoo  found  almost  in  all  the  location,  a  total  of  26  individuals  were  found  at  the 
survey location. 
5.5.2 Trigger Species Population Trends (CCB, GL3.2, GL3.3) 
As  defined  in  the  CCB  Standards,  trigger  species  must meet the criteria of “vulnerability” or 
“irreplaceability”. Vulnerability  is  defined  as regular occurrence  of  IUCN  Red  List  of threatened 
species (species listed as CR, EN, or VU) in the project area, while irreplaceability is defined as 
the presence of 1-5% of a species’ global population (at any stage of the species’ life cycle) in 
the  project  area.  The  project’s  initial  biodiversity survey  identified  at  least  31  species  (13 
mammals, seven birds, one reptile, four fish, and six plants) that are classified as threatened by 
the  IUCN  Red  List  in  the  project  area  and  therefore  meet  the  vulnerability criteria  and  are 
considered  as  trigger  species (table  below). The  project  selected  three  trigger  species  that 
are  endemic  to Maluku  Region to  be  monitored  more intensively  (to  population  density  level), 
namely   the Purple-naped   Lory   (Lorius   domicella), Salmon-crested   Cockatoo   (Cacatua 
moluccensis), and Palaka (Hibiscus pseudotiliaceus). Total species in the location is 289 species 
and the HCV is 67 species will be monitored regularly using standardized protocols (e.g., point 
transect  surveys  for  birds,  camera  trap  surveys  for  mammals, permanent  vegetation  plots  for 
plants, etc.) to determine species occurrence and abundance in the project area.  
 
Trigger species Purple-naped Lory (Lorius domicella) 
Population trend at 
start of project 
The species is endemic to the Seram Island, Ambon, and possibly 
Haruku and Saparua, South Maluku, Indonesia. In the IUCN Red List 
classified  its  species  as  Endangered  and  the  population  trend  is 
decreasing. The initial survey recorded at least 3 individuals found 
in two locations out of 6 survey sites 
Without-project 
scenario 
Without  the  project,  the  species  is  suspected  to  be  experiencing 
rapid  population  decline  due  to  continuous  and  heavy  capture  for 
domestic trade. This is because this species has a very high selling 
value.  The  population  decline  is  also  due  to  habitat  degradation 
such  as  illegal  logging,  settlements,  and  other  major  threats.  This 
species is mostly found in mountains with altitudes between 900-
1,050  m, but  in  the PT Strata area  this  species  was  found at  less 
than  250  meters  above  sea  level. Since  this  bird  has  a  habitat 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
186 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
preference  for  higher  elevations,  forest  cover  in  hilly  areas  is  very 
important  for  this  bird (Birdlife  International,  2016;  Dickinson, 
2003).  
 
With-project scenario With this project, there will be several efforts to protect this species 
involving   multi-stakeholders.   The   protection   of   this   species  is 
carried  out  with  several  sustainable  approaches.  The  involvement 
of stakeholders is necessary. This species is monitored by involving 
stakeholders  such  as  community  patrol  teams,  fire  awareness 
community  (Masyarakat  Peduli  Api/MPA)  forest  management  unit 
(Kesatuan  Pengelolaan  Hutan/KPH)  teams,  and  natural  resource 
conservation centres (Balai Konservasi Sumber Daya 
Alam/BKSDA). To standardize patrol activities SOPs will be created 
for  each  patrol  activity  (SMART  Patrol,  forest  fire  patrol,  etc.). 
Additionally,  to  address  threats  from  deliberate  forest  fires  and 
natural  disasters,  we  will  define  clear  area  boundaries  to  prevent 
overlapping  land  use  and  inform  stakeholders  around  the  project 
area  about  the  project  boundary  and  the  importance  of  this 
species.  
Illegal  hunting  of  Maluku  cockatoos  occurs  due  to  several  factors 
such  as  illegal  wildlife  trading  and  personal  purposes  (trophy  or 
pet). This will happen due to a lack of knowledge at the community 
level   on   the   importance   of   this   species.   Therefore,   active 
awareness-raising   is   necessary.   Furthermore,   increased   law 
enforcement  in  the  field  needs  to  be  further  supported. To  divert 
poaching  in the  project  area,  it  is  necessary  to  increase  livelihood 
options for the community. 
 
Trigger species Salmon-crested Cockatoo (Cacatua moluccensis) 
Population trend at 
start of project 
The  species  is  endemic  to  endemic  to  eastern  Indonesia.  In  the 
IUCN   Red   List   classified   its   species   as   Vulnerable   and   the 
population trend is decreasing. The initial survey recorded at least 
26 individuals found in all survey sites (six transects). 
Without-project 
scenario 
Without  the  project,  the  species  is  suspected  to  be  experiencing 
rapid  population  decline  due  to  continuous  and  heavy  capture  for 
domestic  trade.  This  is  because  this  Cockatoo  has a  very  high 
selling   value.   The   population   decline   is   also   due   to   habitat 
degradation  such  as  illegal  logging,  settlements,  and  other  major 
threats. In the survey sites, this species was common in areas with 
forest cover. The abundance of this species is positively associated 
with the presence of strangler fig trees and large trees suitable for 
nesting (Kinnaird, O'Brien, & Lambert, 2003).

Trigger species Palaka (Hibiscus pseudotiliaceus) 
Population trend at 
start of project 
The IUCN Red List has not assessed the conservation status of this 
species.  The  initial  survey  recorded  2  individuals.  In  the  local 
community of Maluku, this species is believed to provide benefits, 
this  species  is  native  to  the  Maluku  Region  and  has  a  limited 
distribution there, according to the Plant of the World database 
48
. 
Without-project 
scenario 
Without  the  project,  the  species  is  likely  to  experience  population 
decline and even extinction due to logging activities, forest fires and 
natural  disasters.  Threats  to  the  population  of  this  species  are 
caused  by  several  factors,  such  as  the  absence  of  monitoring 
activities,  limited law  enforcement,  land  ownership  that  is  still 
traditional and  has no official  boundaries,  limited  livelihoods, and 
limited understanding of sustainable use of natural resources.

APPENDIX 1: STAKEHOLDER DESCRIPTION TABLE  
 
Stakeholder Rights, interest, and overall relevance to the project 
Raja Negeri (Head Village) 
The Village Head plays the role of the first village decision maker in interventions in the village. The village 
head's interest is in the welfare of the village. The Village Head will be the main policy maker in community 
intervention regarding project activities. 
BPN (Badan Permusyawaratan 
Negeri)/ Saniri/ village 
consultative council 
The BPN will play a role in accommodating and channeling the aspirations of the Village community and 
supervising the performance of the Village Head. Relationship to the project is as one of the decision 
makers at the village level. 
Ketua Adat/Kepala Mata 
Rumah (Costumary Figure) 
Customary leaders are usually the original clan within the village, the customary leader is the ultimate 
decision-maker within the customary land. The traditional leader oversees the administrative lands within 
the project area. His role will be very important within the village. 
Youth Group 
Youth groups have a high interest in opening up job opportunities in the village and they also have a great 
interest in the forest, especially in gardens and hunting in the forest. Youth groups are one of the targets of 
the program for recruiting forest patrol workers and research guides and ecotourism. 
Farmer Group 
Farmer groups that still depend on their livelihoods on perennial crops, some of them plant in the project 
area and they have a high interest in the forest that still provides forest fruits that they use for additional 
income. Farmer groups are part of the project for the planting and agricultural development program in the 
village. 
Fishermen Group Fishermen groups have more interest in the sea area around the village. The relationship with the project 
area will be very small, but the interests for the program in the village will be quite high because the 
fishermen group contains poor people who are the target of the income-increasing program in the village. 
Logger The logger group has a high interest in the forest, they make wood as additional income. This group is 
included in the affected group that will be the target of the program. 

      CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
191 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Dinas Pertanian/ Agriculture 
Department District 
The Department of Agriculture has an interest in agricultural development in project villages. The 
agricultural development program will also involve the Department of Agriculture in program identification, 
program assistance and training for farmer groups. 
Dinas Pendidikan/ Education 
Department District 
The education department is the determinant of the level of education in the villages in the project area. 
Programs around education will involve the education office in project involvement. 
Dinas Kesehatan/ Health 
Department District 
The health department determines the health programs that run around the villages in the area. Their 
involvement in the health program will be a must in the implementation of the project so that project 
activities can be in line with the national health office work plan. 
Oil Mining Company (Citic) The company's territory overlaps with the project area, resulting in overlapping land. Project involvement to 
embrace mining companies is a must to ensure that there are no activities that are detrimental to the 
project, such as logging. 
Galian C (River stone mining 
entrepreneur) 
The stone mining area intersects with the project area, although many activities are carried out in the river, 
the impact on the forest area around the river must be minimized so as not to have a negative impact on 
the project. 
Kesatuan Pemangku Hutan 
(KPH) or Forestry Agency  
KPH is a representative organization of the Ministry of Forestry at the district level, they are decision 
makers in the forest area around SBT. The project will involve them in every activity from the beginning of 
the project. 
BKSDA BKSDA is a representative of the Ministry of Forestry in the aspect of animal protection at the district level, 
the involvement of BKSDA in animal protection projects is very important to participate in the socialization 
and strengthening of the role of BKSDA in the daily lives of communities around the project.
